          <div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">

           <br><sup>4</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Romanian_leu" title="Romanian leu">leu</a> was redenominated on July 1, 2005. As of that date 10,000 (old) lei (ROL) = 1 (new) leu (RON).
           <br><sup>5</sup> The <a href="/wiki/.eu" class="mw-redirect" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as in other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states.
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><b>Romania</b> (old spelling: <b>Rumania</b>, <b>Roumania</b>; <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i lang="ro">România</i>, <small>IPA:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:IPA">[ro.mɨˈni.a]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in southeastern <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> It is north of the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a>, on the Lower <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube River</a>. Part of Romania is circled by the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>. It also has a border on the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Most of the <a href="/wiki/Danube_Delta" title="Danube Delta">Danube Delta</a> is found inside Romania. Romania shares borders with <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> to the far northeast, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Moldova">Republic of Moldova</a> to the near northeast, and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> to the south. </p>
      <p>Romania is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>. It was created when <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> joined together in 1859. It was given its <a href="/wiki/Romanian_War_of_Independence" title="Romanian War of Independence">independence</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin_(1878)" title="Treaty of Berlin (1878)">Treaty of Berlin of 1878</a>. At the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, some of its land (close by what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>) was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> fell in <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution_of_1989" title="Romanian Revolution of 1989">1989</a> Romania was liberated from the communist regime. During the <a href="/wiki/2000s" class="mw-redirect" title="2000s">2000s</a>, Romania made changes to the country, such as reform the <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> system, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> acts, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a> acts, <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">law</a>. That let Romania <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Romania_to_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession of Romania to the European Union">join the European Union</a> on January 1, 2007. </p>
      <p>Romania has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Union_member_states_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of European Union member states by area">9th biggest area of land</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Union_member_states_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of European Union member states by population">7th biggest population</a> (with 19 million people<sup id="cite_ref-recensamantromania.ro_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recensamantromania.ro-2">[2]</a></sup>) of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_member_state" title="European Union member state">European Union member states</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Capital_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (city)">capital</a> and biggest <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a> in Romania is <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i lang="ro">București</i> <span class="IPA audiolink nounderlines" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/71/Ro-Bucure%C8%99ti.ogg" class="internal" title="Ro-București.ogg">/bu.kuˈreʃtʲ/</a></span> <span class="metadata audiolinkinfo"><small>(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="extiw" title="w:Wikipedia:Media help">help</a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Ro-Bucure%C8%99ti.ogg" title="File:Ro-București.ogg">info</a>)</small></span>), with a <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> of 1.6 million. One of the cities in Transylvania, <a href="/wiki/Sibiu" title="Sibiu">Sibiu</a>, was named a <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Romania joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> on March 29, 2004. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Origin">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Origin">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The word <i>Romania</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Rumania" class="mw-redirect" title="Rumania">Rumania</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Rom%C3%A2nia" class="mw-redirect" title="România">România</a></i>) comes from the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a> word <i>Român</i>, which comes from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i>Romanus</i> which means "<a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> English <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/text" class="extiw" title="wikt:text">texts</a> still used the word <i>Rumania</i> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. This came from the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> word <i>Roumanie</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_the_Romans">Prehistory and the Romans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Prehistory and the Romans">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Prehistory and the Romans">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Some of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">human</a> remains found in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> were discovered in Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> They were about 42,000 years old. This may have been when the first <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a> came to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The world's first and oldest <a href="/wiki/Writing" title="Writing">writing</a> comes from people who lived in today's Romania. Approximately 5300 years BC. According to <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeology</a> it is not a matter of symbols, but the world's first writings. It belonged to the Vinča culture which inhabited all of today's Serbia with over 150 Vinča sites and minor parts of Western Romania, northwestern Bulgaria, eastern Bosnia and Herzegovina and Southeastern Hungary. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:REmpire-Dacia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/REmpire-Dacia.png/350px-REmpire-Dacia.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/REmpire-Dacia.png 1.5x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="296"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:REmpire-Dacia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Roman province of Dacia in red.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> in the fourth book of <a href="/wiki/Histories_(Herodotus)" title="Histories (Herodotus)">The Histories</a>, written in about 440 <small><a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">BC</a>/<a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">BCE</a></small>. Herodotus wrote that the <a href="/wiki/Getae" title="Getae">Getae</a> were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Empire" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Persian Empire">Persian</a> Emperor <a href="/wiki/Darius_I_of_Persia" title="Darius I of Persia">Darius the Great</a> when he battled the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The Getae were called the <a href="/wiki/Dacians" title="Dacians">Dacians</a> by the Romans. They were <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a> who were living in <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">Dacia</a>, which is where Romania, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> and the northern part of <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> are now. The Dacians attacked the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a>, the border of which was formed by the Danube, in 87 <small><a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>/<a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE</a></small>. This was during Emperor <a href="/wiki/Domitian" title="Domitian">Domitian</a>'s rule. The Dacians were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> under Emperor <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a> in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trajan%27s_Dacian_Wars&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Trajan's Dacian Wars (not yet started)">two battles</a> that lasted from 101 <small><a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>/<a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE</a></small> until 106 <small><a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>/<a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE</a></small>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The Roman Empire made Dacia into the province of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Dacia" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Dacia">Roman Dacia</a>. </p>
      <p>A lot of <a href="/wiki/Ore" title="Ore">ore</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a>, were found in Roman Dacia.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> A lot of gold and silver were found in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Carpathians" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Carpathians">Western Carpathians</a>. Trajan went back to Rome with 165 tons (330,000 pounds) of gold and 330 tons (660,000 pounds) of silver after his <a href="/wiki/Conquest" class="mw-disambig" title="Conquest">conquest</a>. </p>
      <p>There were many Romans living in the province of Roman Dacia.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> They spoke <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a>. They began to write the local languages using the Latin <a href="/wiki/Alphabet" title="Alphabet">alphabet</a>. Writing languages with the Latin alphabet is called <a href="/wiki/Romanization" title="Romanization">romanization</a>. This became the first version of Romanian.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 3rd century, the province was attacked by groups of <a href="/wiki/Nomad" class="mw-redirect" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> people like the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>. They made the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> leave <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">Dacia</a> about 271 <small><a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">AD</a>/<a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">CE</a></small>. This became the Roman Empire's first <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/abandoned" class="extiw" title="wikt:abandoned">abandoned</a> province.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/origin" class="extiw" title="wikt:origin">origin</a> of modern Romanians is widely talked about by <a href="/wiki/Historians" class="mw-redirect" title="Historians">historians</a> to this day. It is thought that the Romanians were formed from large <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/ethnic" class="extiw" title="wikt:ethnic">ethnic</a> groups that came from both the south and north parts of the Danube.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_Ages_and_Middle_Ages">Dark Ages and Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Dark Ages and Middle Ages">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Dark Ages and Middle Ages">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional"> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">

       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

         </div> 
        </div></li> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">

           <a href="/wiki/File:Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/86px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png" decoding="async" width="86" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/128px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/171px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="245" data-file-height="343"></a>

       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:36px auto;">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Bran_Castle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bran_Castle.jpg/120px-Bran_Castle.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="78" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bran_Castle.jpg/180px-Bran_Castle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bran_Castle.jpg/240px-Bran_Castle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="380" data-file-height="246"></a>
          </div>

         <div class="gallerytext"> 
          <p><a href="/wiki/Bran_Castle" title="Bran Castle">Bran Castle</a> </p> 
         </div> 
        </div></li> 
      </ul> 
      <p>From 271 to 275, the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> took over the abandoned Roman province.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> They lived in <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">Dacia</a> until the 4th century, when another group of wandering peoples, the <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, came to Dacia.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gepids" title="Gepids">Gepids</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gepids_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepids-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Avars" title="Eurasian Avars">Avars</a>, with the Slavic people,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> were in control of <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> through the 8th century. In the 8th century, however, the country was taken over by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hungarian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hungarian Empire (not yet started)">Hungarian Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gepids_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gepids-28">[28]</a></sup> It was made part of the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a>, which ended Romania's Dark Ages. </p>
      <p>The Bulgarians held Transylvania until the 11th century. The <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Cumans" title="Cumans">Cumans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and the Uzes were a few of the people later noted in the history of Romania. </p>
      <p>In 1310, now called the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basarab_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Basarab I">Basarab I</a> started the Romanian principality of <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> was begun by <a href="/wiki/Drago%C5%9F" title="Dragoş">Dragoş</a> around 1352.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, Romanians were living in three different areas: Wallachia (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i>Ţara Românească</i>—"Romanian Land"), Moldavia (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i>Moldova</i>), and <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>. </p>
      <p>Transylvania belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> from around the 10th century until the 16th century,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> when it turned into the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Transylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality of Transylvania">Principality of Transylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> This lasted until 1711.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> had been on the border of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> since the 14th century. As the Ottoman Empire's influence grew, it gradually fell under the <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> (control) of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in the 15th century. </p>
      <p>The best known ruler of this period was <a href="/wiki/Vlad_III_the_Impaler" title="Vlad III the Impaler">Vlad III the Impaler</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/Vlad_Dracula" class="mw-redirect" title="Vlad Dracula">Vlad Dracula</a>, or <i><span class="Unicode">Vlad Ţepeş</span></i>, <small>IPA:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" class="mw-redirect" title="Help:IPA">['tsepeʃ]</a></span>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Wallachia" title="List of rulers of Wallachia">Prince</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a>, during the years of 1448, 1456–62, and 1476.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> While he was the leader of his people, he had an agreement with the Ottoman Empire to stay independent. Many people in Romania during this time thought of him as a ruler with a great sense of justice<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and defense for his country. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> was at its greatest when <a href="/wiki/Stephen_III_of_Moldavia" title="Stephen III of Moldavia">Stephen the Great</a> was ruling between 1457 and 1504.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> He was a great <a href="/wiki/Military" title="Military">military</a> leader, winning 47 battles and losing only 2.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> After every battle he won, Stephen would build a <a href="/wiki/Church" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Church">church</a>. Because he won 47 of the battles that he fought, he ended up building 48 churches.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> After Stephen the Great's death, <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> came under the <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> during the 16th century. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_monarchy">Independence and monarchy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Independence and monarchy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Independence and monarchy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>When Transylvania was the organic part of the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>, and the Ottoman Empire was in control of <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, almost all of the Romanians had limited rights as a citizen.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> They stayed this way even when they made up most of the people in those areas.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After Wallachian Revolution of 1821 as in the 1830s was addressed <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalists</a> thoughts and feelings into Romania and became called <i>"National awakening of Romania'"'. Even then adopted a 3-colored flag, blue-yellow-red, which was later to become a <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Romania" title="Flag of Romania">Flag of Romania</a>.</i> </p>
      <p>After the even more violent <a href="/wiki/European_Revolutions_of_1848" class="mw-redirect" title="European Revolutions of 1848">Revolution of 1848</a> did not <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/succeed" class="extiw" title="wikt:succeed">succeed</a>, so explained the Great Powers did not like the idea of Romania becoming a free nation and it was not a real possibility. </p>
      <p>The people who voted in 1859 in Moldavia and Wallachia picked the same person – <a href="/wiki/Alexander_John_Cuza" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander John Cuza">Alexandru Ioan Cuza</a> – to be the <a href="/wiki/Prince" title="Prince">prince</a> in those areas.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> He managed to unite the people and <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> was seen as a useful method. </p>
      <p>Alexandru Ioan Cuza walked with cautious steps he was not proclaiming a declaration of independence immediately because he knew it would bring a new war. Instead he let Moldavia and Wallachia merged in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Principalities&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United Principalities (not yet started)">United Principalities</a> of the Ottoman Empire and increasing self-government to a greater degree. </p>
      <p>The new union was at the front of today's Romania. With cautious steps we freed itself more and Bucharest was established as the capital. However, farmers had more land when serfdom was abolished, which led to a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> against the Alexandru Ioan Cuza staged by peasants who overthrew the regime. </p>
      <p>Prince Karl of <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a> became the new leader, and was later called <a href="/wiki/Carol_I_of_Romania" title="Carol I of Romania">Prince Carol I of Romania</a>. While the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)">Russo-Turkish War</a> was happening, Romania battled on the Russian side.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> When the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin_of_1878" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Berlin of 1878">Treaty of Berlin of 1878</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> was signed, the <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">Great Powers</a> made Romania an <a href="/wiki/Romanian_War_of_Independence" title="Romanian War of Independence">independent</a> state.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In return, they had to give Russia three of their southern <a href="/wiki/District" title="District">districts</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>. In 1881, the <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principality</a> became a <a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">kingdom</a>, with Prince Carol ruling as King Carol I. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_World_Wars_and_the_Great_Leaders">The World Wars and the Great Leaders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: The World Wars and the Great Leaders">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: The World Wars and the Great Leaders">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: World War I">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: World War I">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>When <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> started in August of 1914, Romania said it was a neutral <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a>. In 1916, the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Allies of World War I">Allies</a> promised to give Romania parts of the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a> where many Romanians lived, if Romania started a war against Austria-Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg/250px-Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg/375px-Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg/500px-Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5310" data-file-height="3880"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Romanian_Officers_WWI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Romanian Army officers in World War I.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Romanian military campaign ended in disaster after Romania's forces were stopped in 1917. Many died. Moldova was one of the few parts of Romania that was not captured when it stopped its attackers in 1917. The Allies won the war, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> had been weakened, and an independent Hungarian republic was proclaimed. As promised, Bessarabia, <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a> and Transylvania became part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Kingdom of Romania</a> in 1918. After the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a> in 1920, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, as agreed, gave up the <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/claim" class="extiw" title="wikt:claim">claims</a> of the Austro-Hungarian Monarchy over Transylvania.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Romania and Bukovina were joined together in 1919 as a <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/result" class="extiw" title="wikt:result">result</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint_Germain" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Saint Germain">Treaty of Saint Germain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Bessarabia joined with Romania in 1920 when the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1920)" title="Treaty of Paris (1920)">Treaty of Paris</a> was signed.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greater_Romania">Greater Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Greater Romania">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Greater Romania">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>After World War I was much bigger and more <a href="/wiki/Nationalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalist">nationalist</a>. The small Kingdom received ("major Transylvania"). The principalities Wallachia, Moldavia and Bessarabia (Moldova) together formed the "Greater Romania" 1918-1940. "Greater Romania" did not survive World War II. </p>
      <p>Romanians called their country <i><a href="/wiki/Rom%C3%A2nia_Mare" class="mw-disambig" title="România Mare">România Mare</a></i>, meaning <i>Great Romania</i> or <i>Greater Romania</i>, in the time between World War I and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. They called it so because it controlled 300,000 square kilometres (115,831&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> of land. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> meant social unrest, high unemployment, strikes and riots, especially a miners' strike in 1929 in Valea Jiului and a strike in Griviţas maintenance workshops. By the mid-1930s, with a recovering Romanian economy, industry grew, although about 80% of Romanians still were engaged in agriculture. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Guard">Iron Guard</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Iron Guard">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Iron Guard">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In end of <a href="/wiki/1930s" title="1930s">1930s</a>, Romania's liberal democracy was slowly being replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist dictatorship</a>. The Archangel Michael Legion, known as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Guard&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Iron Guard (not yet started)">Iron Guard</a> organization, was led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Corneliu_Codreanu_Zelea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Corneliu Codreanu Zelea (not yet started)">Corneliu Codreanu Zelea</a>. In 1937 elections the party supported <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> and got 15.5% of the votes and became the third biggest party. In 1938 king <a href="/wiki/Carol_II_of_Romania" title="Carol II of Romania">Carol II of Romania</a> seized power over Romania. He dissolved all political parties and executed Corneliu Codreanu Zelea along with 12 other leaders. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: World War II">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: World War II">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional"> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:15px auto;">

       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

           <a href="/wiki/File:%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg/120px-%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="86" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg/180px-%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg/240px-%D7%A4%D7%95%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%9D_%D7%99%D7%90%D7%A9%D7%99_5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="939" data-file-height="675"></a>
          </div>
         </div>

          <p>"Death" in <a href="/wiki/Iasi" class="mw-redirect" title="Iasi">Iasi</a> </p> 
         </div> 
        </div></li> 
      </ul> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Carol_II_of_Romania" title="Carol II of Romania">Carol II of Romania</a> declared the country as neutral when <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> broke out in 1939, but included since the Soviet Union occupied Bessarabia and northern Bukovina an alliance with <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Hitler's Germany</a>. This occurred after field marshal <a href="/wiki/Ion_Antonescu" title="Ion Antonescu">Ion Antonescu</a> forced the <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a> Carol II of Romania to abdicate. Antonescu appointed himself "conducator", Romania's dictator, and signed at the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">November 23 of 1940</a> three-powers pact with Nazi Germany. Hitler's Germany was dependent on a continuous importation of <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a> and crude <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> from the Romanian oil fields of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ploesti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ploesti (not yet started)">Ploesti</a>. In 1940, yjr <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> took over the legitimate domination in Northern <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> to the end of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. </p>
      <p>The country's troops fought together with the German Wehrmacht against the Soviet Union. In summer of 1941, Romania join Hitler's war against the Soviet Union in combination also <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> join Hitlers war. Romania built <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" title="Concentration camp">concentration camps</a> and began conducting a <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">massive persecution of Jews</a>, of which became very extreme in the city of Iasi. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holocaust_in_Romania">Holocaust in Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Holocaust in Romania">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Holocaust in Romania">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Romania participated in the Holocaust. The author of the book "The Destruction of the European Jews" Raul Hilberg writes follow: "There was / ... / moment when the Germans actually had to intervene and slow the speed with which the Romanian measures were taken." The hunt for Jews in eastern Romania (including Bessarabia, Bukovina, Transnistria and the city of Iasi) had more the character of pogroms than the German, well-organized camps and transport. </p>
      <p>There were pogroms in the city of Iasi. The homes for the Jewish minority in Iasi were marked with crosses. On June 27, 1941, Ion Antonescu make a phone call with the city's mayor and Antonescu said into the phone: "clean the city <a href="/wiki/Iasi" class="mw-redirect" title="Iasi">Iasi</a> from the Jews." And the Holocaust in Romania has began. Police officers and many civilians went to every Jewish home marked with a cross in the town and murdered thousands of Jews on the same day. </p>
      <p>In June 1941, the Romanian dictator Ion Antonescu gave an "illegal secret order" to the special police force. He ordered the police in cooperation with the Romanian Army and the German SS troops to kill all Jews in east Romania within the next coming years. The Jews living on the countryside was being killed right on the spot. The Jews in the cities were first collected in the ghettos and later deported away. </p>
      <p>On October 22, 1941 the Soviet union with bombs blow up the Romanian military headquarters in Odessa, and killed 66 Romanian soldiers. As revenge Ion Antonescu decided that for every dead Romanian officer, 200 Soviet communists must be killed and for each dead soldier, 100 communists must be killed. All other Communists were imprisoned and Jewish families were taken hostage in the hope that the partisan movement would cease its operations.<sup id="cite_ref-levandehistoria.se_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-levandehistoria.se-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-romania.bloggsida.se_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romania.bloggsida.se-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The day after in Bucharest, on October 23, 1941, around 5 000 people and the majority were Jews was arrested who later executed by <a href="/wiki/Hanging" class="mw-disambig" title="Hanging">hanging</a>. In the Soviet village <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalnik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dalnik (not yet started)">Dalnik</a>, almost 20,000 Jews were incarcerated in to several locked buildings and burned alive.<sup id="cite_ref-levandehistoria.se_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-levandehistoria.se-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-romania.bloggsida.se_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romania.bloggsida.se-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the massacre, many of the Jews who remained in <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> were sent to various concentration camps. Nearby <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> on October 25, 1941, approximately 40,000 Jews, was gathering together on a special closed military secured area, and the Jews had to stay outdoors for more than ten days without food or supply. Many died of cold and starvation. The survivors were murdered one month later.<sup id="cite_ref-levandehistoria.se_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-levandehistoria.se-56">[56]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-romania.bloggsida.se_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romania.bloggsida.se-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Totally approximately 469,000 Jews had been murdered by the military and police in Romania between 1941-1944, including the 325,000 murdered Jews in <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_war">End of war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: End of war">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: End of war">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>At the end of 1943, the Red Army liberated most of Soviet territory and started advancing westward from its borders to defeat Nazi Germany and its allies. It was in this context that the Soviet forces crossed Romania. If the Soviet Union could hit Romania, Nazi Germany's last hope is gone, said the military leadership of the Red Army. Russians deposited the entire 1.5 million soldiers in the attack against Romania and Romania last reserves consisting only of 138 000 soldiers. During the summer of 1944 it began the attack on Bessarabia (Moldova) and the Romanian army fled the area. On 2 August, the whole Bessarabia (Moldova) is captured by the Red Army. The Russians then went a long way in Romania and on 23 August they reached into the Romanian capital Bucharest. The public opinion turned in the country against Antonescu and of summer 1944 he was deposed and imprisoned. The new government signed a ceasefire and extradited itself to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. The Red Army killed the members from the old fascist regime (including <a href="/wiki/Ion_Antonescu" title="Ion Antonescu">Ion Antonescu</a>) on June 1, 1946. </p>
      <p>At the end of the war, Romania was allowed to keep the whole of <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> in west and <a href="/wiki/Dobruja" title="Dobruja">Dobruja</a> from south, but lost <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>/<a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Odessa_Oblast" title="Odessa Oblast">Odessa Oblast</a> in the east (with rich oil reserves) which became parts of the Soviet Union. <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a> was split in half because in the north part the majority ethnic group was Ukrainian and in the south part Romanian. </p>
      <p>The Soviet Union replaced the royal <a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">monarchy</a> with a communist regime in 1947. The Soviet Union took the country's resources, which led to increased <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a> in Romania. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania_and_communism">Romania and communism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Romania and communism">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Romania and communism">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg/125px-Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg.png" decoding="async" width="125" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg/188px-Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg/250px-Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="474" data-file-height="584"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_PCR.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The coat of arms of the Communist party in Romania.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Michael I abdicated the throne and had to leave Romania in 1947 because of the Communists. Romania changed from a monarchy into a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Soviet Socialist Republics">USSR</a> occupied Romania until the late 1950s, when Soviet troops left Romania. During this time, resources in Romania were taken by the Soviet Union due to agreements made by Communist leaders. </p>
      <p>After the Soviet troops left Romania, <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Ceau%C5%9Fescu" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolae Ceauşescu">Nicolae Ceauşescu</a> wanted Romania to become more independent from Moscow. Romania started following slightly different foreign <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/policy" class="extiw" title="wikt:policy">policies</a> than Moscow. After the <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> in 1967, Romania began talks with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and started <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/relation" class="extiw" title="wikt:relation">relations</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Romania started to have their own relations with <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> countries. Romania officials were allowed to participate in peace talks between Israel and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and between Israel and the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The national debt Romania owed to other countries went from $3 billion to almost $10 billion between 1977 and 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The amount of money that Romania owed other countries caused them to <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/rely" class="extiw" title="wikt:rely">rely</a> on banks and other lenders from around the world. President Nicolae Ceauşescu's <a href="/wiki/Autarky" title="Autarky">autarchic</a> ways meant he did not want to rely on other countries and Romania paid back money borrowed from other countries. This affected the Romanian economy. To try to stay in power, Ceauşescu had anyone who disagreed with him arrested and put in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Many people were killed or hurt. Almost 60,000 people were put in <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">psychiatric hospitals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Ceauşescu eventually lost power and was killed in the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution_of_1989" title="Romanian Revolution of 1989">Romanian Revolution of 1989</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989_to_2007">1989 to 2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: 1989 to 2007">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Change section: 1989 to 2007">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1989, the National Salvation Front came into power. It was led by <a href="/wiki/Ion_Iliescu" title="Ion Iliescu">Ion Iliescu</a>. When they came into power, several other <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/party" class="extiw" title="wikt:party">parties</a> from before World War II were remade. These included the <a href="/wiki/Christian-Democratic_National_Peasants%27_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian-Democratic National Peasants' Party">Christian-Democratic National Peasants' Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberal_Party_(Romania)" title="National Liberal Party (Romania)">National Liberal Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Social_Democrat_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian Social Democrat Party">Romanian Social Democrat Party</a>. In April 1990, as a result of several <span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/rally"><span style="color: #CC2200;" title="rally (Page does not exist on Wiktionary)">rallies</span></a></span>, <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/protest" class="extiw" title="wikt:protest">protests</a> started. The people who protested did not <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/recognize" class="extiw" title="wikt:recognize">recognize</a> the results of the <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/election" class="extiw" title="wikt:election">election</a>. This was because they thought that members of the National Salvation Front were communists. More and more people protested, and it became a demonstration – a very big protest. This was called the <a href="/wiki/Golaniad" title="Golaniad">Golaniad</a>, and it became very violent. </p>
      <p>When the National Salvation Front lost power, several other parties were made. These were the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Partidul_Social_Democrat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Partidul Social Democrat (not yet started)">Social Democratic Party</a>, the Democratic Party, and a couple of other parties from before the war. The Social Democratic Party ruled Romania from 1990 until 1996. Ion Iliescu was the head of state, or person in charge. After 1996, several other parties came into power and lost it. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Traian_B%C4%83sescu" title="Traian Băsescu">Traian Băsescu</a> became the president. </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, Romania became closer friends with <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. In 2004, Romania joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and hosted the 2008 summit.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The country applied in June 1993 for membership in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and became an Associated State of the EU in 1995, an Acceding Country in 2004, and a member on January 1, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Romania" title="Geography of Romania">Geography of Romania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg/260px-Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg/390px-Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg/520px-Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="577"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Physical_map_of_Romania.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Map" title="Map">physical map</a> of Romania.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Romania is a part of southeastern Europe. It borders the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube River</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> lie in the center. </p>
      <p>Romania is the biggest country in southeast <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> by population. It has an <a href="/wiki/Area" title="Area">area</a> of 238,391 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">square kilometres</a> (92,043&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">sq&nbsp;mi</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_in_order_of_geographical_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of European countries in order of geographical area">twelfth-largest</a> country in Europe. Most of Romania's border with <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> is made by the Danube. The Danube joins the <a href="/wiki/Prut_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Prut River">Prut River</a>. The Prut River makes the <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldovan</a>–Romanian border. The Danube then flows into the area of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> inside Romania. This makes the <a href="/wiki/Danube_Delta" title="Danube Delta">Danube Delta</a>. The <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">delta</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a> <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/reserve" class="extiw" title="wikt:reserve">reserve</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Some of the other major rivers in Romania are the <a href="/wiki/Siret_River" title="Siret River">Siret</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Olt_River" title="Olt River">Olt</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mure%C5%9F_River" title="Mureş River">Mureş</a>. The Siret River runs from the north to the south of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>. The Olt River runs from the Carpathian Mountains to <a href="/wiki/Oltenia" title="Oltenia">Oltenia</a>. The Mureş runs through Transylvania from the east to the west. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landscape">Landscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=16" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Landscape">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Change section: Landscape">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The land in Romania is made up of equal parts of mountains, hills, and low-lying areas. The Carpathian Mountains make up a big part of the center of Romania. <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountain_peaks_in_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mountain peaks in Romania">Fourteen of its mountain ranges</a> are taller than 2,000&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (6,562&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a>). The tallest mountain in Romania is <a href="/wiki/Moldoveanu_Peak" title="Moldoveanu Peak">Moldoveanu Peak</a>, with a peak altitude of 2,544&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Metre" title="Metre">m</a> (8,346&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers">Rivers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=17" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Rivers">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Change section: Rivers">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Danube is the longest <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">river</a> in Romania. Its <a href="/wiki/Length" title="Length">length</a> inside Romania is about 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Kilometre" title="Kilometre">kilometres</a> (621&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">mi</a>). That is almost half of the length of the entire Danube. Almost all of the rivers in Romania are either <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/direct" class="extiw" title="wikt:direct">direct</a> or <span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/indirect"><span style="color: #CC2200;" title="indirect (Page does not exist on Wiktionary)">indirect</span></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> of the Danube. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weather">Weather</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=18" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Weather">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Change section: Weather">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Romania has a <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> that changes between <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate climate">temperate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a> climates. The reason for the climate changes is because Romania is near the coast. Romania has four different seasons. The average temperature during the year is 11&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (51.8&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>) in southern Romania and 8&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (46.4&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>) in the northern part.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Lots of rain and snow falls on the highest western mountains. Most of this falls as <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a>. In the southern parts of the country, the amount of rain and snow that falls is around 60 <a href="/wiki/Centimetre" title="Centimetre">centimetres</a> (23.6&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Inch" title="Inch">in</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The lowest temperature ever taken in Romania was −38.5&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (−37.3&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>), at <a href="/wiki/Bra%C5%9Fov" title="Braşov">Braşov</a> in 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-temperature_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-temperature-73">[73]</a></sup> The highest temperature ever recorded in Romania was 44.5&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a> (112.1&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Fahrenheit" title="Fahrenheit">°F</a>), near <a href="/wiki/Calafat" title="Calafat">Calafat</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1950s" title="1950s">1950s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-temperature_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-temperature-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=19" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Society">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Change section: Society">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_and_culture">Language and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=20" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Language and culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Change section: Language and culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/official" class="extiw" title="wikt:official">official</a> language of Romania is <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>. The Romanian language is an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Romance_languages" title="Eastern Romance languages">Eastern Romance language</a>. </p>
      <p>Romania has its own culture because of where it is found. It is the point where 3 different areas meet: <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>. Romanian culture is a mix of all these areas.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The culture of Romania was influenced by the Greeks, Romans, and Slavs.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=21" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Religion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Change section: Religion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Romania is a <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a> <a href="/wiki/State" title="State">state</a>. This means Romania has no <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">national religion</a>. The biggest religious group in Romania is the Romanian Orthodox Church. It is an <a href="/wiki/Autocephaly" title="Autocephaly">autocephalous</a> church inside of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> <a href="/wiki/Full_communion" title="Full communion">communion</a>. In 2002, this religion made up 86.7% of the population. Other religions in Romania include <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> (4.7%), <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (3.7%), <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostalism</a> (1.5%) and the Romanian Greek-Catholicism (0.9%).<sup id="cite_ref-census_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-80">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=22" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Cities">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Change section: Cities">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <p><a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (city)">capital</a> of Romania. It also is the biggest <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">city</a> in Romania, with a population of over 2 millions peoples.<sup id="cite_ref-insse.ro_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insse.ro-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are 5 other cities in Romania that have a population of more than 300,000 people. These are <a href="/wiki/Ia%C5%9Fi" class="mw-redirect" title="Iaşi">Iaşi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timi%C5%9Foara" title="Timişoara">Timişoara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constan%C5%A3a" title="Constanţa">Constanţa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Craiova" title="Craiova">Craiova</a>. Romania also has 5 cities that have more than 200,000 people living in them: <a href="/wiki/Gala%C5%A3i" title="Galaţi">Galaţi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bra%C5%9Fov" title="Braşov">Braşov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ploie%C5%9Fti" title="Ploieşti">Ploieşti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Br%C4%83ila" title="Brăila">Brăila</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oradea" title="Oradea">Oradea</a>. </p>
      <p>Thirteen other cities in Romania have a population of more than 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=23" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional"> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
        <div style="width: 155px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
          <div style="margin:30px auto;">
