      <p>Romania joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> on January 1, 2007. Romania's <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a> is healthy. Currently, Romania makes around $350 billion in <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">Gross domestic product</a> and a <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> of $16,540.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Long into the 1900s, Romania was still a largely agricultural country. During Communism 1947-1989, the country had planned economy. The transition from planned economy to a market economy after the communist regime led to economic collapse in the 1990s, the reasons was that more money was printed, expensive prices and substantial privatization of the companies, which initially leads to skyrocketing unemployment. The reforms in the 1990s allowed foreign investors for the first time to buy land in Romania. When it was going explosively good for the industry in the Latin countries such as <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, these countries began to trade with Romania because it is favorite voice country for them to grow in. Foreign companies expanding in Romania since then, and spurs the market. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=24" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Education">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Change section: Education">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The Romanian school is obligatory for 10 years. Children also have the opportunity to be part of a voluntary pre-school at an early age 3–6 years. After school, students can voluntarily take the entrance exam to high school, which has a range of practical and theoretical lines. There are over 40 higher educational institutions, including five universities and five technical colleges. Tuition is free and is a hot political commitment even at the university. The country's minorities have the opportunity to receive instruction in their native language. Since 1989, education has been reformed. But it has been slow and the standard of education varies greatly in different parts of the country, education has improved the standard of urban compared to rural areas where quality can be very low. Romania participates fully in the EU's education program.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_welfare">Social welfare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=25" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Social welfare">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Change section: Social welfare">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> rate in Romania is five per-cent and has been low for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The living standards were very low at the end of the Communist era, but the situation was just only improved a little bit during the 1990s. On the contrary, the living significantly due caused by the large privatization of jobs that resulted in high unemployment and rising prices. In later years lived yet 2010 nearly 10 percent of the population in absolute poverty<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and of these, 90% live in rural areas. The State social insurance system have relatively broad coverage but resources are extremely small. </p>
      <p>Reforms have been initiated and in 1999 the health insurance became privatized and paid by the employers and the employees. Several thousand local trade unions were founded after the revolution, which were later amalgamated (combined) into federations. These unions and federations have helped organise students, pensioners and the unemployed; because these groups of people all have similar needs, concerns and goals. </p>
      <p>By the first quarter of 2011 the average monthly household income is 2,318 <a href="/wiki/Romanian_leu" title="Romanian leu">Romanian leu</a> (equivalent to approximately £862 USD). The different between <a href="/wiki/Countryside" class="mw-redirect" title="Countryside">countryside</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> may vary the income is 36 per-cent higher in the urban area than in the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The pension system is reformed.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The most worrying thing is the fact that there are more pensioners than the number of working people. because many who dismissed during the privatizations had per-retirement. Romanian Pensioners average pension at the month is at about 190 euros (equivalent to approximately £250-300 USD). The current low average retirement age (55 years for men and 57 years for women) will be gradually increased until 2014, when it gets 60 years for women and 65 years for men. </p>
      <p>Many of the country's Gypsies have no identity cards and are therefore excluded from the social benefit systems, schools and health care. The State-run health care is free, but the care system is neglected and has deteriorated in recent years due to lack of resources and underpaid staff. In many cases,the patients paying "under the table" to get treatment. here is evidence to suggest that a patient's wealth plays an important role in how they receive medical treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=26" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Science and technology">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Change section: Science and technology">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Traian_Vuia_aircraft.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Traian_Vuia_aircraft.jpg/220px-Traian_Vuia_aircraft.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/Traian_Vuia_aircraft.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="293"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Traian_Vuia_aircraft.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Traian_Vuia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Traian Vuia (not yet started)">Traian Vuia</a>, early flight pioneer
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Historically, Romanian researches and inventors have made notable contributions to several fields, such as: <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">aeronautics</a>, medicine, mathematics, computer science/engineering, physics, biophysics, chemistry, <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">biochemistry</a> and biology. In the history of flight, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Traian_Vuia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Traian Vuia (not yet started)">Traian Vuia</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aurel_Vlaicu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aurel Vlaicu (not yet started)">Aurel Vlaicu</a> built and flew some of the earliest successful aircraft, while <a href="/wiki/Henri_Coand%C4%83" title="Henri Coandă">Henri Coandă</a> discovered the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coand%C4%83_effect&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coandă effect (not yet started)">Coandă effect</a> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fluidics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fluidics (not yet started)">fluidics</a>. Preceding him, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Elie_Carafoli&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Elie Carafoli (not yet started)">Elie Carafoli</a> was a pioneering contributor to the field of aerodynamics in the world. </p>
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Victor_Babe%C5%9F&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Victor Babeş (not yet started)">Victor Babeş</a> discovered more than 50 germs and a cure for a disease named after him, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Babesiosis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Babesiosis (not yet started)">babesiosis</a>; biologist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicolae_Paulescu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nicolae Paulescu (not yet started)">Nicolae Paulescu</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a>. Another biologist, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Emil_Palade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Emil Palade (not yet started)">Emil Palade</a>, received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> for his contributions to <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">cell biology</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Constantinescu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="George Constantinescu (not yet started)">George Constantinescu</a> created the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Theory_of_sonics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Theory of sonics (not yet started)">theory of sonics</a>, while <a href="/w/index.php?title=Laz%C4%83r_Edeleanu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lazăr Edeleanu (not yet started)">Lazăr Edeleanu</a> was the first chemist to synthesize <a href="/wiki/Amphetamine" title="Amphetamine">amphetamine</a> and also invented the modern method of <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">refining</a> <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Costin_Neni%C5%A3escu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Costin Neniţescu (not yet started)">Costin Neniţescu</a> found new methods for the synthesis of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pirilium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pirilium (not yet started)">pirilium</a> salts, of <a href="/wiki/Carbene" title="Carbene">carbenes</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tryptamine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tryptamine (not yet started)">tryptamine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serotonin" title="Serotonin">serotonin</a>, two new syntheses for the indole nucleus, and a new method of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Polymerisation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Polymerisation (not yet started)">polymerisation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ethylene" title="Ethylene">ethylene</a>. </p>
      <p>Several <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematicians</a> distinguished themselves as well, among them: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gheorghe_%C5%A2i%C5%A3eica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gheorghe Ţiţeica (not yet started)">Gheorghe Ţiţeica</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spiru_Haret&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Spiru Haret (not yet started)">Spiru Haret</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Grigore_Moisil&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Grigore Moisil (not yet started)">Grigore Moisil</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Miron_Nicolescu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Miron Nicolescu (not yet started)">Miron Nicolescu</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicolae_Popescu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nicolae Popescu (not yet started)">Nicolae Popescu</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=%C5%9Etefan_Odobleja&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ştefan Odobleja (not yet started)">Ştefan Odobleja</a>; the latter is also regarded as the ideological father behind <a href="/wiki/Cybernetics" title="Cybernetics">cybernetics</a>. </p>
      <p>Notable physicists and inventors also include: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Horia_Hulubei&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Horia Hulubei (not yet started)">Horia Hulubei</a> in atomic physics, <a href="/w/index.php?title=%C8%98erban_%C8%9Ai%C8%9Beica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Șerban Țițeica (not yet started)">Șerban Țițeica</a> in theoretical physics, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mihai_Gavril%C4%83&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mihai Gavrilă (not yet started)">Mihai Gavrilă</a> specialized in quantum theory and discoverer of the <a href="/wiki/Atom" title="Atom">atomic dichotomy</a> phenomenon, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexandru_Proca&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alexandru Proca (not yet started)">Alexandru Proca</a> (known for the first meson theory of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_forces&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nuclear forces (not yet started)">nuclear forces</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Proca%27s_equations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Proca's equations (not yet started)">Proca's equations</a> of the vectorial mesonic field), <a href="/w/index.php?title=%C5%9Etefan_Procopiu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ştefan Procopiu (not yet started)">Ştefan Procopiu</a> known for the first theory of the <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_moment" title="Magnetic moment">magnetic moment</a> of the electron in 1911 (now known as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bohr-Procopiu_magneton&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bohr-Procopiu magneton (not yet started)">Bohr-Procopiu magneton</a>), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Theodor_V._Ionescu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Theodor V. Ionescu (not yet started)">Theodor V. Ionescu</a>, the inventor of a multiple-cavity <a href="/wiki/Magnetron" class="mw-redirect" title="Magnetron">magnetron</a> (1935), a hydrogen <a href="/wiki/Maser" title="Maser">maser</a> in 1947, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stereoscopy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stereoscopy (not yet started)">3D imaging</a> for cinema/television in 1924 and hot deuterium plasma studies for controlled <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fusion" title="Nuclear fusion">nuclear fusion</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ionel_Solomon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ionel Solomon (not yet started)">Ionel Solomon</a> known for the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_magnetic_resonance" title="Nuclear magnetic resonance">nuclear magnetic resonance</a> theory in solids, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_Overhauser_effect&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nuclear Overhauser effect (not yet started)">Solomon equations</a><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> devices, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Petrache_Poenaru&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Petrache Poenaru (not yet started)">Petrache Poenaru</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nicolae_Teclu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nicolae Teclu (not yet started)">Nicolae Teclu</a> and Victor Toma, with the latter known for the invention and construction of the first Romanian computer, the CIFA-1 in 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The nuclear physics facility of the European Union's proposed <a href="/w/index.php?title=Extreme_Light_Infrastructure&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Extreme Light Infrastructure (not yet started)">Extreme Light Infrastructure (ELI)</a> laser will be built in Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Romania currently has 1,400 <a href="/wiki/Watt" title="Watt">MW</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> capacity by means of one active <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">nuclear power plant</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Cernavod%C4%83_Nuclear_Power_Plant&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cernavodă Nuclear Power Plant (not yet started)">Cernavodă</a>) with 2 reactors, which constitutes around 18% of the national power generation capacity of the country. This makes Romania <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_power_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nuclear power by country (not yet started)">the 23rd largest user of nuclear power in the world</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=27" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Change section: Government">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=28" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Change section: Politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Romania" title="Constitution of Romania">Constitution of Romania</a> is found to be based from the Constitution of France's Fifth Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-Europaworld_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europaworld-96">[96]</a></sup> It was passed into law on December 8, 1991. after a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" class="mw-redirect" title="Referendum">referendum</a> was held.<sup id="cite_ref-Europaworld_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europaworld-96">[96]</a></sup> 73 <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/amendments" class="extiw" title="wikt:amendments">amendments</a> were added to the constitution in October of 2003 to bring the constitution of Romania up to code with the constitution of the European Union. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a> of the Romanian government is known as the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Romania" title="Parliament of Romania">Parliament</a>. It contains two chambers – the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Romania" title="Senate of Romania">Senate</a>, containing 140 members, and the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Romania">Chamber of Deputies</a>, which has 346 members.<sup id="cite_ref-Europaworld_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europaworld-96">[96]</a></sup> The members of both chambers are elected every four years through party-list proportional representation.<sup id="cite_ref-Europaworld_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europaworld-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial branch">judicial branch</a> of the Romanian government is separate from the other branches. It is made up of a <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/system" class="extiw" title="wikt:system">system</a> of courts. The court with the most authority is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=High_Court_of_Cassation_and_Justice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="High Court of Cassation and Justice (not yet started)">High Court of Cassation and Justice</a>, which is the supreme court of Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Other courts, including appeal, county, and local courts also make up the judicial branch of the Romanian Government. The way the system of courts works in Romania is modelled off of the French model of law.<sup id="cite_ref-Europaworld_96-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europaworld-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> It is based on <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisions">Divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=29" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Divisions">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Change section: Divisions">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Romania is divided into <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Romania" title="Counties of Romania">41 counties</a>, including the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, which is also its own county. </p>
      <p>Romania is <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/divide" class="extiw" title="wikt:divide">divided</a> further into 319 <a href="/wiki/Cities_of_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Cities of Romania">cities</a> and 2,686 <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Romania" title="Communes of Romania">communes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Each of the communes has its own council that is led by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Army">Army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=30" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Army">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Change section: Army">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Romanian Army is made up of <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Land_Forces" title="Romanian Land Forces">Land</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Romanian Air Force (not yet started)">Air</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Romanian_Naval_Forces&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Romanian Naval Forces (not yet started)">Naval Forces</a>, which are all led by a <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-chief</a>. The commander-in-chief is given orders by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Romania)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Defense (Romania)">Ministry of Defense</a>. During war, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Romania" title="President of Romania">President</a> leads the Army. 90,000 people were in the Romanian Army in 2003: 15,000 civilians and 75,000 military people. Of the 75,000 military people in the Romanian Army, 45,800 are in the land forces, 13,250 are in the air forces, 6,800 are in the naval forces, and 8,800 in other areas of the military.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_pages">Related pages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=31" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Related pages">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Change section: Related pages">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=32" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: References">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Change section: References">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
